<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">A broadband center-fed ultra-high frequency (UHF) near-field radio frequency identification (RFID) reader antenna is proposed and investigated in this letter. The design utilizes four tapered double-side parallel stripline (TDSPSL)-fed dipoles to form a circular loop to achieve broadband impedance matching and strong and uniform magnetic field distribution. Parametric studies are carried out to characterize the design concept. The proposed antenna was fabricated and measured. The measured 10-dB impedance bandwidth is 236 MHz (814-1050 MHz), which covers the entire UHF RFID frequency band. The maximum reading distance is 210 mm at 30 dBm input power. Moreover the antenna can achieve a 100% read percentage within the height of 135 mm for multitag detection. The measured results agree well with the simulated ones.</div>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Radio frequency identification (RFID) technology has been developed rapidly in the past decades. It has been widely used in identifying and tracking objects <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>. Recently, ultra-high frequency (UHF) near-field RFID technology has received much attention due to its excellent performance for detecting objects surrounded by metals or liquids in item-level RFID applications such as bottles of water, retail goods, luxury goods, and pharmaceuticals <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_1">[14]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_1">[15]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_1">[16]</a>. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_1">[17]</a>, the item-level RFID is also used in the tracking of small-size living animals for the behavior analysis. The UHF near-field RFID system requires a special antenna that can generate strong and uniform magnetic field in its interrogation zone.</p><p>In UHF RFID frequency band, the electromagnetic wavelength is much smaller than those in low-frequency (LF) and high-frequency (HF) bands. Conventional solid-line-based LF or HF RFID reader antenna design technology <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a> cannot be used in designing an electrically large UHF near-field antenna. Various UHF near-field RFID reader antennas have been proposed and investigated over the past few years. A lumped capacitor-loaded loop antenna was reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>. An electrically large zero-phase-shift line grid-array antenna was presented in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>. It has a wide bandwidth and larger interrogation zone, however the 100% read percentage is achieved within 13.5 mm. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_1">[14]</a>, a power-divider-fed dipole array was presented to generate strong magnetic field. Although the power divider is used, its bandwidth is narrow (7 MHz). Some other techniques such as oppositely directed currents <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>, dual-printed dipoles <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a>, traveling-wave structure <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a>, left-handed metamaterial loading <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a>, and fractal technique <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_1">[15]</a> are used to design UHF near-field antennas.</p><p>In this letter, a broadband center-fed UHF near-field RFID reader antenna is presented and analyzed. The antenna is composed of four tapered double-sided parallel stripline (TDSPSL)-fed dipoles. The TDSPSL is used to broaden the impedance bandwidth of the antenna. Simulation results show that the antenna generates strong and uniform magnetic field distribution within its interrogation zone. A prototype antenna was fabricated and measured. The measured 10-dB impedance bandwidth is 25.3% (814–1050 MHz), which covers the entire UHF RFID frequency band. The maximum reading distance is 210 mm at 30 dBm input power. Moreover, the antenna can achieve a 100% read percentage within the height of 135 mm for multitag detection.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Antenna Structure and Parametric Study</h2></div><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a> shows the configuration of the proposed broadband center-fed UHF near-field RFID reader antenna. The basic unit cell of the antenna is a TDSPSL-fed dipole. Four dipoles form a circular loop. The inner area of the circular loop is the designed interrogation zone. Each dipole's arms are printed on the upper and lower surfaces of the substrate, respectively. </p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Configuration of the broadband center-fed UHF near-field RFID reader antenna: (a) top view; (b) side view.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6975018/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a> shows the simulated current distribution of the proposed antenna at 900 MHz. As can be seen, the current along the circular loop is kept in phase. Such current distribution generates strong and uniform magnetic field over the interrogation zone. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a> plots the simulated vertical magnetic field curves along <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-19-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-197" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-198"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-199" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-19">x</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-axis at the height of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-200" role="math" style="width: 5.649em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.048em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1005.05em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-201"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-202"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-203"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-204" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-205" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-206" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">10</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-207" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-208"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-209"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-210" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-20">{Z} = 10 ~\hbox{mm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The input power of the antenna is 30 dBm in the simulation. It is observed that the proposed antenna generates a uniform magnetic field distribution with maximum variation of 5 dB for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-21-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-211" role="math" style="width: 11.354em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 10.213em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1010.21em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-212"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-213" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-214" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">76</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-215" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-216"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-217"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-218" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-219" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">≤</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-220" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.303em;">X<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-221" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">≤</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-222" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">76</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-223" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-224"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-225"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-226" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-21">-76~\hbox{mm} \leq X \leq 76~\hbox{mm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> within 860–960 MHz. The magnetic field strength difference is only 1.8 dB at 860 and 960 MHz. These indicate that the proposed antenna can generate strong, uniform, and stable magnetic field distribution at UHF RFID frequency band.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>Simulated current distribution of the proposed antenna at 900 MHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6975018/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>

<p></p><p>Parametric studies are carried out to characterize the proposed center-fed UHF near-field RFID reader antenna. Only one parameter is changed, while the other parameters are kept unchanged unless indicated.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a> shows the simulated reflection coefficients as a function of frequency for different arm length <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-241" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.68em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-242"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-243"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-244"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-245"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-246" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-247"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-248"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-249" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-250" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-251" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-24">{L_{\rm arc}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. It can be seen that the impedance bandwidth shifts downward as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-252" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.68em 2.526em -999.997em); position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-257" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-258"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-259"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-260" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-261" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-262" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-25">{L_{\rm arc}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> increases from 51 to 61 mm. This is because a large dipole arm length should have a lower resonant frequency.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>Simulated reflection coefficient of the proposed antenna for different values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-263" role="math" style="width: 2.186em; <p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a> plots the simulated reflection coefficient curves for different input widths (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-27-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-274" role="math" style="width: 1.505em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.32em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-275"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-276"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-277"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-278"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.02em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-279" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">W<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-280"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-281"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-282" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-27">{W_{\rm s}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) of TDSPSL. It is clear that the impedance matching is strongly affected by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-28-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-283" role="math" style="width: 1.505em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.32em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-284"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-285"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-286"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-287"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.02em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-288" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">W<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-289"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-290"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-291" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-28">{W_{\rm s}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. As <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-29-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-292" role="math" style="width: 1.505em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.32em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-293"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-294"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-295"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-296"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.02em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-297" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">W<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-298"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-299"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-300" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-29">{W_{\rm s}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> decreases, the impedance bandwidth first gets wide, then gets narrow. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a> shows the simulated reflection coefficient curves for different output widths (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-30-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-301" role="math" style="width: 1.505em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.32em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-302"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-303"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-304"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-305"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.02em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-306" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">W<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-307"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-308"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-309" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-30">{W_{\rm e}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) of TDSPSL. It is observed that the matching is strongly affected by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-310" role="math" style="width: 1.505em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.32em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-311"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-312"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-313"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-314"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.02em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-315" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">W<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-316"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-317"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-318" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-31">{W_{\rm e}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as well. As <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-319" role="math" style="width: 1.505em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.32em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-320"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-321"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-322"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-323"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.02em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-324" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">W<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-325"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-326"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-327" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">{W_{\rm e}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> increases, the impedance bandwidth gets wide first, then gets narrow too. These mean that the changing tendency of impedance bandwidth is regular. Actually, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-328" role="math" style="width: 1.505em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.32em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-329"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-330"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-331"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-332"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.02em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-333" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">W<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-334"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-335"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-336" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">{W_{\rm s}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-337" role="math" style="width: 1.505em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.32em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-338"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-339"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-340"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-341"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.02em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-342" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">W<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-343"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-344"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-345" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">{W_{\rm e}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> affect the characteristic impedance of the TDSPSL, thus affecting the impedance of the antenna. By selecting appropriate dimensions of the TDSPSL, the proposed antenna can achieve good impedance matching.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Simulated reflection coefficients of the proposed antenna for different values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-346" role="math" style="width: 1.723em; <div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p>Simulated reflection coefficients of the proposed antenna for different values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-355" role="math" style="width: 1.723em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.326em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1001.33em 2.517em -999.997em); overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.136em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.833em; left: 0.929em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-361"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-362"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-363" style="font-size: 70.7%; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.246em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.254em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">{W_{\rm e}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6975018/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>In summary, the arm length of the dipole (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-364" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.68em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-365"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-366"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-367"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-368"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-369" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-370"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-371"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-372" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-373" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-374" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-37">{L_{\rm arc}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) affects the resonant frequency of the antenna. The TDSPSL dimensions (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-375" role="math" style="width: 1.505em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.32em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-376"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-377"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-378"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-379"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.02em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-380" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">W<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-381"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-382"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-383" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">{W_{\rm s}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-384" role="math" style="width: 1.505em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.32em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-385"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-386"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-387"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-388"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.02em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-389" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">W<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-390"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-391"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-392" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-39">{W_{\rm e}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) affect the impedance matching of the antenna.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Measurements and Results</h2></div><p>A prototype of the proposed antenna was fabricated with the same dimensions as the simulated ones. The reflection coefficient of the prototype was measured using Agilent E5071C network analyzer. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a> shows the simulated and measured reflection coefficients of the prototype. The measured 10-dB bandwidth (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-393" role="math" style="width: 7.33em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.61em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1006.55em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-394"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-395" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-396"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-397"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-398"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-399" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-400"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-401"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-402" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">11</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-403" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-404" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">&lt;</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-405" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">−</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-406" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">10</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-407" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-408"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-409"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-410" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">dB</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">\vert{S_{11}}\vert &lt; - 10~\hbox{dB}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) is 25.3% (814–1050 MHz), which agrees well with the simulated result.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>Simulated and measured reflection coefficients of the proposed antenna.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6975018/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>In order to verify the near-field performance of the antenna, near-field tag-detecting experiments have been conducted by using Imping Speedway Revolution reader R220 and Impinj button tag J41. The J41 tag is a commercial Monza 4 microchip tag <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_3">[18]</a> using a 6-mm-radius (out radius) loop antenna. The read sensitivity of the chip is −17.4 dBm. Identifying the tag J41 requires the component of the magnetic field <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-411" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.26em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-412"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-413"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-414"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-415"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.9em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-416" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-417" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-41">{H_z}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (normal to the surface of the antenna) to be at least -24 dBA/m. The measurement setup is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>. In the experiments, we used two test methods. One is single tag measurement as described in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_3">[6]</a>; the other is multitag measurement as described in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_3">[16]</a>. By using single tag measurement, we put a tag on the slider of a form ruler and record the reading distances by moving the ruler within the area of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-418" role="math" style="width: 7.33em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.61em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1006.61em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-419"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-420" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">200</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-421" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-422" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">200</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-423" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-424"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.68em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-425"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-426"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-427" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.685em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-428"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-429"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-430" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">200\times 200~\hbox{mm}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. By using multitag measurement, we put 25 tags on a foam board uniformly within the interrogation zone and record the number of readable tags by changing the height of the foam board.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Photograph of the proposed antenna and its near-field performance measurement setup.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6975018/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a> shows the simulated vertical magnetic field distribution and measured readable area of the antenna at different heights of 100, 140, and 160 mm. The wire frames represent the metal part of the antenna. The single tag measurement method is used in the tests. The input power in the measurement is 30 dBm. As can be seen, the measured readable areas of the antenna agree well with the simulated ones.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig><p>Simulated vertical magnetic distribution (color sections) and measured readable area (black sections) in horizontal plane of the antenna at different heights: (a) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-431" role="math" style="width: 6.617em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.228em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.392em 1005.23em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-432"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-433"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-434"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-435" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; padding-left: 0.268em;">140</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-449" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-450"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-451"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-452" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.228em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.392em 1005.23em 2.45em -999.997em); overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.069em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-458" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-459" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">160</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-460" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-461"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-462"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-463" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">{Z} = 160~\hbox{mm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6975018/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a> plots the measured read percentage against reading distance of the antenna by considering a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-464" role="math" style="width: 7.39em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.67em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1006.67em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-465"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-466" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">200</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-467" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-468" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">200</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-469"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-470"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-471"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-472"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-473" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">-mm</span></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-474"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-475"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-476"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.847em 1000em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-477"></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-478" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-46">200 \times 200{\hbox{-mm}}{^2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> interrogation area concentric with the antenna and divided into <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-479" role="math" style="width: 3.607em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.246em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.19em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-480"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-481" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">20</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-482" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-483" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">20</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-47">20 \times 20</script></tex-math></inline-formula> cells of sizes <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-484" role="math" style="width: 4.688em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.207em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1004.21em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-485"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-486" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-487" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-488" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">1</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-489" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-490"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-491"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-492"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-493"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-494" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">cm</span></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-495"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-496"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-497"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.847em 1000em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-498"></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-499" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-48">1 \times 1~{\hbox{cm}}{^2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. As can be seen, by using single tag measurement, the maximum reading distance reaches 210 mm, and a 100% read percentage within the whole antenna surface (circle of radius 80 mm) is achieved within the height of 160 mm. However, by using multitag measurement, the height of 100% tag detection is decreased to 135 mm. This is caused by the interaction between the tags.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-10-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-10-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 10. </b><fig><p>Measured read percentage of the proposed antenna at different heights using two methods.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6975018/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 11</a> shows the tested result of eight stacked tags on the antenna surface by using the method in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_3">[3]</a>. The tags are separated by 1.5-cm-thick foam layers (the first tag has been placed directly in contact with the surface of the antenna). The overall height of the stacked tags is 10.5 cm. The total number of the detected tags has been recorded, when varying the stack position on the antenna surface. Almost all the eight tags are read in each cell of the antenna surface grid (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-49-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-500" role="math" style="width: 4.688em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.207em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1004.21em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-501"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-502" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-503" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-504" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">1</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-505" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-506"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-507"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-508" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">cm</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-509"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-510"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-511"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.847em 1000em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-512"></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-513" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-49">1 \times 1~\hbox{cm}{^2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>). However the read performance gets worse at borders of the antenna. This is caused by two reasons: One is the interaction between tags; the other is the magnetic strength at borders are weaker than the magnetic strength at the central area of the antenna.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-11-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6975018/6975018-fig-11-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 11. </b><fig><p>Number of detected tags in a 10-s time interval, for different positions of eight stacked tags on the antenna surface.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6975018/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>A broadband center-fed UHF near-field RFID reader antenna has been proposed in this letter. Its basic structure is a TDSPSL-fed dipole. Four TDSPSL-fed dipoles form a circular loop. The inner area of the circular loop is the designed interrogation zone. The measured impedance bandwidth is 25.3% (814–1050 MHz). The measured maximum reading distance is 210 mm at 30 dBm input power. Furthermore, the 100% read percentage can be achieved within the height of 135 mm by using multitag measurement. Therefore, the antenna shows good performance in UHF near-field RFID applications.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

j$('document').ready(function(){
	if(getCookie('legacyUserName')!=null)
	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>
